<p><b>Roberto Mancini</b> (<small>Italian pronunciation: </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Italian" title="Help:IPA for Italian">[roˈbɛrto manˈtʃiːni]</a></span>; born 27 November 1964) is an Italian <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> manager and former player, who last managed <a href="/wiki/Inter_Milan" title="Inter Milan">Internazionale</a>. As a player, Mancini played as a <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)#Second_striker" title="Forward (association football)">deep-lying forward</a>, and was best known for his time at <a href="/wiki/U.C._Sampdoria" title="U.C. Sampdoria">Sampdoria</a>, where he played more than 550 matches, and helped the team win the <a href="/wiki/Serie_A" title="Serie A">Serie A</a> league title, four <a href="/wiki/Coppa_Italia" title="Coppa Italia">Coppa Italia</a> titles, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Cup_Winners%27_Cup" title="European Cup Winners' Cup">European Cup Winners' Cup</a>. He was capped 36 times for <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_football_team" title="Italy national football team">Italy</a>, taking part at <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1988" title="UEFA Euro 1988">UEFA Euro 1988</a> and the <a href="/wiki/1990_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1990 FIFA World Cup">1990 FIFA World Cup</a>, achieving semi-final finishes in both tournaments. In 1997, after 15 years at Sampdoria, Mancini left the club to join <a href="/wiki/S.S._Lazio" title="S.S. Lazio">Lazio</a>, where he won a further <i><a href="/wiki/List_of_Italian_football_champions" title="List of Italian football champions">Scudetto</a></i>, as well as the Cup Winners' Cup, the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Super_Cup" title="UEFA Super Cup">UEFA Super Cup</a> and two more Coppa Italia titles.</p>
<p>As a player, Mancini would often give team talks at <a href="/wiki/Half-time" title="Half-time">half-time</a>. Towards the end of his playing career he became an assistant to <a href="/wiki/Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson" title="Sven-Göran Eriksson">Sven-Göran Eriksson</a> at Lazio.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> His first manager role was at a cash-stricken <a href="/wiki/ACF_Fiorentina" title="ACF Fiorentina">Fiorentina</a> at only 35 years old. He won a Coppa Italia there, but left with the team facing bankruptcy. Months later he took over as manager at Lazio, where again he inherited financial constraints and was forced to lose a number of key players. With limited resources during his two-season tenure, he guided the club to another Coppa Italia.</p>
<p>In 2004, Mancini was given the chance to manage a major club with more resources when he was offered the manager's job at Inter. During his first tenure at Inter, the club won three consecutive Serie A titles, an Inter club record, and an <a href="/wiki/Football_records_in_Italy#Most_consecutive_wins" title="Football records in Italy">Italian record 17 consecutive league game victories</a> stretching nearly half a season; Mancini became Inter's most successful manager in 30 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> Despite his domestic success, many pundits saw the repeated failure to win the coveted <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> as the main reason for his dismissal in 2008.</p>
<p>After being out of football for over a year, Mancini was appointed <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a> manager in December 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tactics_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-tactics-4">[4]</a></sup> Under his stewardship, he instilled a winning culture at the club taking Manchester City from a mid-table club to the pinnacle of English football, combining defensive solidity with attacking flair. In the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_in_English_football" title="2010–11 in English football">2010–11 season</a>, his first full season at Manchester City, Mancini guided the club to Champions League football and the <a href="/wiki/2011_FA_Cup_Final" title="2011 FA Cup Final">FA Cup</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_in_English_football" title="2011–12 in English football">2011–12 season</a>, Mancini guided Manchester City to the club's first league title in 44 years in an enthralling last day of the season, winning 3–2, with two goals in <a href="/wiki/Last-minute_goal" title="Last-minute goal">injury time</a> in what was called "the best match of the best last day of the season in English football history."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> Under Mancini, Manchester City progressed to the <a href="/wiki/2013_FA_Cup_Final" title="2013 FA Cup Final">2013 FA Cup Final</a>, but were defeated by <a href="/wiki/Wigan_Athletic_F.C." title="Wigan Athletic F.C.">Wigan Athletic</a> 1–0.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> Mancini was sacked on 13 May 2013,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> and in September of that year took over at Turkish club <a href="/wiki/Galatasaray_S.K._(football)" title="Galatasaray S.K. (football)">Galatasaray</a>, winning the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Cup" title="Turkish Cup">Turkish Cup</a> in his only season at the club.</p>
<p>Mancini has won a total of 25 trophies, 13 as a player and 12 as a manager. Regarded as a cup specialist,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Mancini has reached at least a semi-final of a major national cup competition in every season he has been a manager, from 2002 to 2013. He holds a number of records including most consecutive <a href="/wiki/Coppa_Italia#Finals" title="Coppa Italia">Coppa Italia finals</a> from 2004 to 2008, with <a href="/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_Coppa_Italia" title="2003–04 Coppa Italia">Lazio once in 2004</a> and with Inter in the following four seasons.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roberto_Mancini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Mancini was born in the small town of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesi" title="Jesi">Jesi</a>, Marche on 27 November 1964,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FACTBOX-Roberto_Mancini_factbox_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-FACTBOX-Roberto_Mancini_factbox-12">[12]</a></sup> but then moved onto the mountain town of <a href="/wiki/Roccadaspide" title="Roccadaspide">Roccadaspide</a> and was raised by Aldo and Marianna Mancini along with his younger sister Stephanie. Raised a Roman Catholic, his young life in the town of Jesi revolved around religion and football.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>He was an altar boy and played for the local Aurora Calcio football team in his youth. On one occasion, a fixture clashed with his first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holy_Communion" title="Holy Communion">Holy Communion</a>. Halfway through the ceremony, the eight-year-old Mancini was nowhere to be seen. His local priest who was administering his first communion frequently <a href="/wiki/Coach_(sport)" title="Coach (sport)">coached football</a>, he heard they were losing 2–0 at half-time and so he asked a young Mancini quietly after receiving his communion if he had his football kit and boots with him. Roberto said they were in the changing rooms and so he told him to sneak out of the side door and put them on because his team needed him, unbeknown to his father.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Playing_career">Playing career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roberto_Mancini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Playing career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sampdoria">Sampdoria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roberto_Mancini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Sampdoria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sampdoria_%2790-91_campione_d%27Italia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="409" data-file-width="712" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Sampdoria_%2790-91_campione_d%27Italia.jpg/220px-Sampdoria_%2790-91_campione_d%27Italia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Sampdoria_%2790-91_campione_d%27Italia.jpg/330px-Sampdoria_%2790-91_campione_d%27Italia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Sampdoria_%2790-91_campione_d%27Italia.jpg/440px-Sampdoria_%2790-91_campione_d%27Italia.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sampdoria_%2790-91_campione_d%27Italia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mancini with <a href="/wiki/U.C._Sampdoria" title="U.C. Sampdoria">Sampdoria</a> during the <a href="/wiki/1990%E2%80%9391_Serie_A" title="1990–91 Serie A">1990–91 Serie A</a> title-winning season.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Mancini debuted in the Italian <a href="/wiki/Serie_A" title="Serie A">Serie A</a> for <a href="/wiki/Bologna_F.C._1909" title="Bologna F.C. 1909">Bologna</a> on 1981.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FACTBOX-Roberto_Mancini_factbox_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-FACTBOX-Roberto_Mancini_factbox-12">[12]</a></sup> The following year, he was bought by <a href="/wiki/U.C._Sampdoria" title="U.C. Sampdoria">Sampdoria</a>, for £2.2 million, whom he played for until 1997.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> With Sampdoria, he formed a dynamic <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)#Striker" title="Forward (association football)">strike</a> partnership with <a href="/wiki/Gianluca_Vialli" title="Gianluca Vialli">Gianluca Vialli</a>, and helped the club to its only <a href="/wiki/List_of_Italian_football_champions" title="List of Italian football champions">league title</a> in <a href="/wiki/1990%E2%80%9391_Serie_A" title="1990–91 Serie A">1991</a>, four <a href="/wiki/Coppa_Italia" title="Coppa Italia">Coppa Italias</a> and a <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Cup_Winners%27_Cup" title="UEFA Cup Winners' Cup">Cup Winners' Cup</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UEFA_Cup_Winners%27_Cup_1989%E2%80%9390" title="UEFA Cup Winners' Cup 1989–90">1990</a>. He also appeared in the <a href="/wiki/1992_European_Cup_Final" title="1992 European Cup Final">final</a> of the <a href="/wiki/1991%E2%80%9392_European_Cup" title="1991–92 European Cup">1991–92 European Cup</a> against <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">Barcelona</a>. At 27, Mancini sat on the interview panel that selected <a href="/wiki/Sven-G%C3%B6ran_Eriksson" title="Sven-Göran Eriksson">Sven-Göran Eriksson</a> as manager. Mancini often delivered the team-talk for Sampdoria. He attended board meetings and had a say in transfer business. In <a href="/wiki/David_Platt_(footballer)" title="David Platt (footballer)">David Platt</a>'s 1995 autobiography, <i>Achieving the Goal</i>, he described the day he met Sampdoria in Genoa while playing for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A.S._Bari" title="A.S. Bari">Bari</a> and, lining up in the tunnel, became aware that Mancini was looking his way. Platt wrote: "I thought nothing of it until he asked me, very matter-of-factly, if I was staying at Bari. Outright he asked if I wanted to join Sampdoria. Mancini had been at the club years and was almost a son to the president, Paolo Mantovani." Mancini kept in touch when Platt moved to <a href="/wiki/Juventus_F.C." title="Juventus F.C.">Juventus</a> and eventually helped bring him to Sampdoria. At that stage, Mancini had established himself as the most powerful voice in the <i>Blucerchiati</i> dressing room.</p>
<p>As a teenager at Sampdoria, Mancini was not someone who liked his authority being questioned. After <a href="/wiki/Trevor_Francis" title="Trevor Francis">Trevor Francis</a> signed from <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a> in 1982, aggrieved that his place was under threat, the 18-year-old Mancini ended up picking a fight with 28-year-old Francis on the training ground. A similar incident occurred with <a href="/wiki/Liam_Brady" title="Liam Brady">Liam Brady</a>, who was eight years older. Additionally, <a href="/wiki/Juan_Sebasti%C3%A1n_Ver%C3%B3n" title="Juan Sebastián Verón">Juan Sebastián Verón</a> tells the story of swearing in Mancini's direction during an argument about a badly-taken corner. After the match, Mancini had stripped off to the waist and was waiting to fight him. "He is not an easy person, you know," Verón says. "He has this complicated personality."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lazio">Lazio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roberto_Mancini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Lazio">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>With <a href="/wiki/S.S._Lazio" title="S.S. Lazio">Lazio</a>, Mancini won his second <a href="/wiki/List_of_Italian_football_champions" title="List of Italian football champions"><i>Scudetto</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Cup_Winners%27_Cup" title="UEFA Cup Winners' Cup">Cup Winners' Cup titles</a>, as well as two more <a href="/wiki/Coppa_Italia" title="Coppa Italia">Coppa Italias</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_Serie_A" title="1999–2000 Serie A">1999–00 season</a>, Lazio won the <i>Scudetto</i> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_Coppa_Italia" title="1999–2000 Coppa Italia">Coppa Italia</a>, but Mancini failed to score in 20 matches and later announced his playing retirement. He joined Lazio's coaching staff as Sven-Göran Eriksson's number two. In 2011, when asked about Mancini, Eriksson said, "I took him to Lazio with me and he wanted to be a manager even while he was a player. He was the coach, he was the kit man, he was the bus driver, everything. At Sampdoria he wanted to check that everything was in place before training. Sometimes I would have to tell him: 'Mancio, you have a game to play on Sunday, you will be exhausted if you have to control everything.' But he was like that."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Leicester_City">Leicester City</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roberto_Mancini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Leicester City">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Joining <a href="/wiki/Leicester_City_F.C." title="Leicester City F.C.">Leicester City</a> on loan in January 2001,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mancini.27s_move_to_Leicester_will_benefit_England_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mancini.27s_move_to_Leicester_will_benefit_England-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mancini.27s_Foxes_fate_in_balance_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mancini.27s_Foxes_fate_in_balance-17">[17]</a></sup> Mancini made his <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> debut against <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> at the age of 36, but failed to complete a full 90 minutes in his five appearances for the club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Just_how_close_were_Leicester_City_to_signing_Dutch_master_Johan_Cruyff.3F_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Just_how_close_were_Leicester_City_to_signing_Dutch_master_Johan_Cruyff.3F-18">[18]</a></sup> In early February, he was given leave of absence, citing personal reasons. He telephoned the club on 14 February, however, and informed them he would not be returning to England; he had been offered the manager's job at <a href="/wiki/ACF_Fiorentina" title="ACF Fiorentina">Fiorentina</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mancini_leaves_Leicester_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mancini_leaves_Leicester-19">[19]</a></sup> Despite this, he cites his time at Leicester City as the period during which he fell in love with the English game, and which later prompted him to accept the job at Manchester City.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_career">International career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roberto_Mancini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: International career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Despite success at club level, Mancini never became a regular for <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_football_team" title="Italy national football team">Italy</a>. At the under-21 level, Mancini was part of the team which reached the semi-finals in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1984_UEFA_European_Under-21_Football_Championship" title="1984 UEFA European Under-21 Football Championship">1984 UEFA European Under-21 Football Championship</a> and finished runners-up in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UEFA_U-21_Championship_1986" title="UEFA U-21 Championship 1986">1986</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-storiedicalcio.altervista.org_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-storiedicalcio.altervista.org-20">[20]</a></sup> He made his <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_under-21_football_team" title="Italy national under-21 football team">international senior squad</a> debut at the age of 19, under <a href="/wiki/Enzo_Bearzot" title="Enzo Bearzot">Enzo Bearzot</a>, on 26 May 1984, in a 2–0 away win against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canada_national_men%27s_soccer_team" title="Canada national men's soccer team">Canada</a> in <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FACTBOX-Roberto_Mancini_factbox_12-2"><a href="#cite_note-FACTBOX-Roberto_Mancini_factbox-12">[12]</a></sup> he later won 36 caps, and scored four goals for his country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-figc.it_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-figc.it-21">[21]</a></sup> Mancini was a starting player at <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1988" title="UEFA Euro 1988">Euro 1988</a>, where Italy reached the semi-finals;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> during the tournament, he scored a goal in a 1–1 draw against hosts <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">West Germany</a>, in the opening match of the tournament on 10 June.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Mancini was also a non-playing member of <a href="/wiki/Azeglio_Vicini" title="Azeglio Vicini">Azeglio Vicini</a>'s Italian squad that finished in third place at the <a href="/wiki/1990_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1990 FIFA World Cup">1990 World Cup</a> on home soil. He was kept out of the side by competition from <a href="/wiki/Gianluca_Vialli" title="Gianluca Vialli">Gianluca Vialli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salvatore_Schillaci" title="Salvatore Schillaci">Salvatore Schillaci</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andrea_Carnevale" title="Andrea Carnevale">Andrea Carnevale</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Baggio" title="Roberto Baggio">Roberto Baggio</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>Mancini's international career ended after a dispute with national team coach <a href="/wiki/Arrigo_Sacchi" title="Arrigo Sacchi">Arrigo Sacchi</a>, when Mancini was upset because he would not be guaranteed a first team place at the <a href="/wiki/1994_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1994 FIFA World Cup">1994 World Cup</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> Fierce competition with other creative forwards for places in the starting line-up, such as <a href="/wiki/Gianfranco_Zola" title="Gianfranco Zola">Gianfranco Zola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Signori" title="Giuseppe Signori">Giuseppe Signori</a>, Roberto Baggio and later <a href="/wiki/Francesco_Totti" title="Francesco Totti">Francesco Totti</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alessandro_Del_Piero" title="Alessandro Del Piero">Alessandro Del Piero</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> hindered his international opportunities, hastening his self-imposed exile from the Italian national team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Style_of_play">Style of play</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roberto_Mancini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Style of play">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Mancini was a creative and technically gifted forward, who was frequently deployed as a <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)#Second_striker" title="Forward (association football)">supporting striker</a> alongside a centre forward, or, on occasion, as an <a href="/wiki/Playmaker#Advanced_playmakers" title="Playmaker">offensive playmaker</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Attacking_midfielder" title="Midfielder">attacking midfield</a> position later on in his career. A classic <a href="/wiki/Squad_number_(association_football)" title="Squad number (association football)">number 10</a> with creativity and vision, as well as accurate passing and finishing ability, he was capable of assisting many goals as well as scoring them himself, due to his eye for the final pass; he was also known for his excellent technique in the air, which enabled him to execute spectacular volleys. An elegant and skilful player, Mancini was also renowned for his flair, ball control and <a href="/wiki/Dribbling#Association_football" title="Dribbling">dribbling</a> ability, as well as his tactical intelligence. He frequently stood out because of this attribute, as well as due to his leadership. He was often a vocal presence on the football pitch, regularly organising and motivating his teammates, as well as discussing with opponents and arguing with referees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> Mancini is regarded as one of the best Italian players of his generation, and as one of Italy's greatest ever number 10s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-storiedicalcio.altervista.org_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-storiedicalcio.altervista.org-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Managerial_career">Managerial career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roberto_Mancini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Managerial career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years">Early years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roberto_Mancini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Early years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Although Mancini had written a research pamphlet entitled <i>"Il Trequartista"</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> which examined the role of an <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Attacking_midfielder" title="Midfielder">attacking midfielder</a>, he had not as yet attained the necessary coaching badges to become a manager. He therefore needed special dispensation from the Italian football authorities to take the post at <a href="/wiki/ACF_Fiorentina" title="ACF Fiorentina">Fiorentina</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> which was given on 4 March 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Roberto_Mancini:_Factfile_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-Roberto_Mancini:_Factfile-35">[35]</a></sup> He was out on loan to Leicester City and returned after four matches to take the Fiorentina job<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FACTBOX-Roberto_Mancini_factbox_12-3"><a href="#cite_note-FACTBOX-Roberto_Mancini_factbox-12">[12]</a></sup> on 26 February 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ACF_Fiorentina_.C2.BB_Manager_history_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-ACF_Fiorentina_.C2.BB_Manager_history-36">[36]</a></sup> Fiorentina was plagued by financial problems and made occasional playing appearances himself. According to various sources,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manchestereveningnews.co.uk_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-manchestereveningnews.co.uk-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Mancini sometimes worked unpaid and even received death threats after key players such as <a href="/wiki/Rui_Costa" title="Rui Costa">Rui Costa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Francesco_Toldo" title="Francesco Toldo">Francesco Toldo</a> had to be sold. Despite this, Mancini managed to win the <a href="/wiki/Coppa_Italia" title="Coppa Italia">Coppa Italia</a> before quitting on 11 January 2002,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Roberto_Mancini:_Factfile_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-Roberto_Mancini:_Factfile-35">[35]</a></sup> after just ten months in the job, with Fiorentina in the relegation zone of Serie A.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manchestereveningnews.co.uk_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-manchestereveningnews.co.uk-37">[37]</a></sup> Fiorentina were ultimately relegated in June 2002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 9 May 2002, Mancini was appointed manager of Lazio.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Roberto_Mancini:_Factfile_35-2"><a href="#cite_note-Roberto_Mancini:_Factfile-35">[35]</a></sup> He was again restricted by financial considerations, having to sell key players such as <a href="/wiki/Hern%C3%A1n_Crespo" title="Hernán Crespo">Hernán Crespo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alessandro_Nesta" title="Alessandro Nesta">Alessandro Nesta</a>, and players were forced to take an 80 percent pay cut. In his first season with Lazio, however, the club reached the <a href="/wiki/2002%E2%80%9303_UEFA_Cup#Semi-finals" title="2002–03 UEFA Cup">semi-finals of the UEFA Cup</a>. In <a href="/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_Serie_A" title="2003–04 Serie A">2003–04</a>, Lazio won the <a href="/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_Coppa_Italia" title="2003–04 Coppa Italia">Coppa Italia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Lazio finished fourth in 2003 and sixth in 2004. Before the start of the <a href="/wiki/2004%E2%80%9305_Serie_A" title="2004–05 Serie A">2004–05 season</a>, rumours circulated in the Italian press that <a href="/wiki/Inter_Milan" title="Inter Milan">Inter Milan</a> had approached Mancini to fill the recently vacated managerial position at the club. Then, in July 2004, Lazio released Mancini from his contract<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FACTBOX-Roberto_Mancini_factbox_12-4"><a href="#cite_note-FACTBOX-Roberto_Mancini_factbox-12">[12]</a></sup> and joined Inter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Roberto_Mancini:_Factfile_35-3"><a href="#cite_note-Roberto_Mancini:_Factfile-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Internazionale">Internazionale</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roberto_Mancini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Internazionale">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roberto_Mancini.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="525" data-file-width="700" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Roberto_Mancini.jpg/220px-Roberto_Mancini.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Roberto_Mancini.jpg/330px-Roberto_Mancini.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Roberto_Mancini.jpg/440px-Roberto_Mancini.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Roberto_Mancini.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mancini pictured in 2004 as Inter manager.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Mancini took over on 7 July 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Roberto_Mancini:_Factfile_35-4"><a href="#cite_note-Roberto_Mancini:_Factfile-35">[35]</a></sup> Under Mancini, Inter soon won the club's first domestic trophy since 1989. Inter became the dominant team in Italy. In Mancini's first season, Inter won the <a href="/wiki/2004%E2%80%9305_Coppa_Italia" title="2004–05 Coppa Italia">Coppa Italia</a> with a 3–0 victory over <a href="/wiki/A.S._Roma" title="A.S. Roma">Roma</a> at the <a href="/wiki/San_Siro" title="San Siro">San Siro</a>. Inter finished third in <a href="/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_Serie_A" title="2003–04 Serie A">2003–04 Serie A</a> and reached the <a href="/wiki/2004%E2%80%9305_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2004–05 UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> <a href="/wiki/2004%E2%80%9305_UEFA_Champions_League#Quarter-finals" title="2004–05 UEFA Champions League">quarter-finals</a> only to be knocked out by city rivals <a href="/wiki/A.C._Milan" title="A.C. Milan">A.C. Milan</a> 3–0 on aggregate.</p>
<p>In August 2005, Inter won the <a href="/wiki/2005_Supercoppa_Italiana" title="2005 Supercoppa Italiana">2005 Supercoppa Italiana</a> for the second time in their history with a 1–0 victory over <a href="/wiki/Juventus_F.C." title="Juventus F.C.">Juventus</a>. Inter again won the <a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_Coppa_Italia" title="2005–06 Coppa Italia">Coppa Italia</a> and <a href="/wiki/2006_Supercoppa_Italiana" title="2006 Supercoppa Italiana">Italian Super Cup</a>. Following the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Calciopoli" title="Calciopoli">Calciopoli</a></i> scandal, <a href="/wiki/Juventus_F.C." title="Juventus F.C.">Juventus</a> were stripped of the <i><a href="/wiki/List_of_Italian_football_champions" title="List of Italian football champions">Scudetto</a></i> title, which was handed to Inter instead. Inter achieved a record-breaking run of 17 consecutive victories in <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_Serie_A" title="2006–07 Serie A">Serie A</a>, starting on 25 September 2006, with a 4–1 home win over <a href="/wiki/A.S._Livorno_Calcio" title="A.S. Livorno Calcio">Livorno</a> and ending on 28 February 2007 after a 1–1 draw at home to <a href="/wiki/Udinese_Calcio" title="Udinese Calcio">Udinese</a>. The run lasted for almost five months and is among the best in <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">European league football history</a>. Inter won a <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_Serie_A" title="2006–07 Serie A">second successive league title</a> with five games to spare and only losing one league game all season. Inter finished with a record-breaking 97 points.</p>
<p>Mancini became the third coach in <a href="/wiki/History_of_Inter_Milan" title="History of Inter Milan">Inter history</a> to win back-to-back league titles after <a href="/wiki/Alfredo_Foni" title="Alfredo Foni">Alfredo Foni</a>; <a href="/wiki/1952%E2%80%9353_Serie_A" title="1952–53 Serie A">1952–53</a> and <a href="/wiki/1953%E2%80%9354_Serie_A" title="1953–54 Serie A">1953–54</a> and <a href="/wiki/Helenio_Herrera" title="Helenio Herrera">Helenio Herrera</a>; <a href="/wiki/1964%E2%80%9365_Serie_A" title="1964–65 Serie A">1964–65</a> and <a href="/wiki/1965%E2%80%9366_Serie_A" title="1965–66 Serie A">1965–66</a>). Inter also progressed to the <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_Coppa_Italia" title="2006–07 Coppa Italia">Coppa Italia</a> and <a href="/wiki/2007_Supercoppa_Italiana" title="2007 Supercoppa Italiana">Italian Super Cup</a> for the third consecutive season, but were beaten in both finals by <a href="/wiki/A.S._Roma" title="A.S. Roma">Roma</a>. Once again, however, Inter struggled in <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">Europe</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2006–07 UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a>, they were knocked out in the <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_UEFA_Champions_League#First_knockout_round" title="2006–07 UEFA Champions League">first knockout round</a> by <a href="/wiki/Valencia_CF" title="Valencia CF">Valencia</a>. At the end of the game, there was a mass brawl involving both sets of players.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> Mancini was not involved in the incident, but camera footage showed him attempting to block a camera's view before he was seen shrugging his shoulders and walking away. This was Mancini's fourth, and final, season in charge of Inter. His reputation continued to grow as he added a third consecutive <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_Serie_A" title="2007–08 Serie A">Serie A title</a> to his honours. Again he guided Inter to the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_Coppa_Italia" title="2007–08 Coppa Italia">Coppa Italia final</a>, but lost for a second consecutive season to Roma, 2–1, at the <a href="/wiki/Stadio_Olimpico" title="Stadio Olimpico">Stadio Olimpico</a>.</p>
<p>Despite his successes, the inability to make any real progress in the Champions League displeased Inter owner <a href="/wiki/Massimo_Moratti" title="Massimo Moratti">Massimo Moratti</a>. Inter were knocked out in the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_UEFA_Champions_League#First_knockout_round" title="2007–08 UEFA Champions League">first knockout round</a> of the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2007–08 UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> by <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FACTBOX-Roberto_Mancini_factbox_12-5"><a href="#cite_note-FACTBOX-Roberto_Mancini_factbox-12">[12]</a></sup> The first leg took place at <a href="/wiki/Anfield" title="Anfield">Anfield</a>, with defender <a href="/wiki/Marco_Materazzi" title="Marco Materazzi">Marco Materazzi</a> being sent off in the 30th minute. Inter almost held out for a draw, but two late goals in the 85th and 90th minute by Liverpool damaged Inter's hopes of progressing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> The return leg was at the <a href="/wiki/San_Siro" title="San Siro">San Siro</a>, but again Mancini was not helped by the ill discipline of his players, with <a href="/wiki/Nicol%C3%A1s_Burdisso" title="Nicolás Burdisso">Nicolás Burdisso</a> being sent off in the 50th minute before <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Torres" title="Fernando Torres">Fernando Torres</a> scored for Liverpool in the 64th minute to seal the tie 3–0 on aggregate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> After being eliminated by Liverpool, Mancini wanted to leave after the season, but changed his mind the following day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FACTBOX-Roberto_Mancini_factbox_12-6"><a href="#cite_note-FACTBOX-Roberto_Mancini_factbox-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>In March 2008, amid rumours that he was to be sacked and replaced by <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a> manager <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mourinho" title="José Mourinho">José Mourinho</a> at the end of the season, Mancini announced his intention to step down at the end of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Serie_A_2007%E2%80%9308" title="Serie A 2007–08">2007–08 season</a>. He rescinded this decision a day later after meeting with Moratti.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fortune_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-fortune-44">[44]</a></sup> On 29 May 2008, however, Inter officially announced the sacking of Mancini.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Inter_Milan_dismiss_coach_Mancini_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-Inter_Milan_dismiss_coach_Mancini-45">[45]</a></sup> Moratti justified the sacking by pointing to Mancini's comments after the Liverpool defeat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mancini_inter_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-mancini_inter-46">[46]</a></sup> He was replaced by Mourinho.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Out_of_football">Out of football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roberto_Mancini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Out of football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Mancini was linked to the vacant Chelsea manager's position in May 2008<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> and then the same role at <a href="/wiki/Notts_County_F.C." title="Notts County F.C.">Notts County</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> On 30 October 2009, Mancini won compensation for his sacking by Inter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> The contract settlement, however, meant Mancini was actually unemployable by any other club from May 2008 to October 2009. It was rumoured that Mancini was entitled to a €16 million pay-off, but in the end, he reportedly settled for €5 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fortune_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-fortune-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Manchester_City">Manchester City</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roberto_Mancini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Manchester City">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2009.E2.80.9310">2009–10</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roberto_Mancini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 2009–10">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 19 December 2009, Mancini was publicly revealed to be taking over as manager of <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a> on a three-and-a-half-year deal following the sacking of <a href="/wiki/Mark_Hughes" title="Mark Hughes">Mark Hughes</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Roberto_Mancini:_Factfile_35-5"><a href="#cite_note-Roberto_Mancini:_Factfile-35">[35]</a></sup> With wealthy Emirati owners who were willing to invest heavily in the team, Manchester City had become a club expectant of success.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> Having been appointed halfway through the season, Mancini's arrival had an immediate impact on City's form, with four consecutive wins.</p>
<p>Mancini won his first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manchester_Derby" title="Manchester Derby">Manchester Derby</a> over <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> 2–1 in a <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Football_League_Cup" title="2009–10 Football League Cup">League Cup</a> <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Football_League_Cup#Semi-finals" title="2009–10 Football League Cup">semi-final</a> <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Football_League_Cup#First_leg" title="2009–10 Football League Cup">first leg</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> United won the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Football_League_Cup#Second_leg" title="2009–10 Football League Cup">second-leg</a> 3–1, however, and eliminated City from the competition. In April, City moved into fourth place in the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Premier_League" title="2009–10 Premier League">Premier League</a>. On 5 May, however, a single goal defeat at home to <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a> meant that City missed out on a <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2010–11 UEFA Champions League">Champions League spot</a>. City finished <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Premier_League" title="2009–10 Premier League">the season</a> in fifth place, their highest <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> finish.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> There had been speculation that Mancini might lose his job if City failed to secure Champions League football, but chairman <a href="/wiki/Khaldoon_Al_Mubarak" title="Khaldoon Al Mubarak">Khaldoon Al Mubarak</a> gave his support to Mancini.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chairman_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-chairman-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2010.E2.80.9311">2010–11</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roberto_Mancini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: 2010–11">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roberto_Mancini_-_Lech_-_Manchester_005.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1067" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Roberto_Mancini_-_Lech_-_Manchester_005.jpg/220px-Roberto_Mancini_-_Lech_-_Manchester_005.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Roberto_Mancini_-_Lech_-_Manchester_005.jpg/330px-Roberto_Mancini_-_Lech_-_Manchester_005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Roberto_Mancini_-_Lech_-_Manchester_005.jpg/440px-Roberto_Mancini_-_Lech_-_Manchester_005.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Roberto_Mancini_-_Lech_-_Manchester_005.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mancini as Manchester City manager in 2010.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Mancini spent heavily during the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Summer_transfer_window&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Summer transfer window (page does not exist)">summer transfer window</a>. He signed German international defender <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A9r%C3%B4me_Boateng" title="Jérôme Boateng">Jérôme Boateng</a> from <a href="/wiki/Hamburger_SV" title="Hamburger SV">Hamburger SV</a> for approximately £10.64 million,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup_Final" title="2010 FIFA World Cup Final">Spanish World Cup winner</a> <a href="/wiki/David_Silva" title="David Silva">David Silva</a> from <a href="/wiki/Valencia_CF" title="Valencia CF">Valencia</a> for approximately £24 million,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Yaya_Tour%C3%A9" title="Yaya Touré">Yaya Touré</a> from <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">Barcelona</a> for around £24 million<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Aleksandar_Kolarov" title="Aleksandar Kolarov">Aleksandar Kolarov</a> from Lazio for approximately £16 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Premier_League" title="2010–11 Premier League">2010–11 Premier League</a> season was marked by runs of mixed form. With a 2–0 win away at <a href="/wiki/Wigan_Athletic_F.C." title="Wigan Athletic F.C.">Wigan Athletic</a> on 19 September 2010, City moved into fourth position in the league and did not drop out of the top four positions during the rest of the season. In October and November, the team struggled for form, which put some pressure on Mancini,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> with his tactics widely criticised following two consecutive 0–0 home draws with Manchester United and <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_City_F.C." title="Birmingham City F.C.">Birmingham City</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>A fine run of form in the weeks running up to Christmas, however, meant City occupied first place in the Premier League twice over the Christmas period. In the ten games before 15 January 2011, City won seven times, drew twice and lost only once as they moved into title contention, while also securing passage into the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_UEFA_Europa_League#Round_of_32" title="2010–11 UEFA Europa League">Round of 32 of the</a> <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_UEFA_Europa_League" title="2010–11 UEFA Europa League">Europa League</a> by finishing as the top team in <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_UEFA_Europa_League#Group_A" title="2010–11 UEFA Europa League">Group A</a>. As a result of his team's strong league form, Mancini was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Manager_of_the_Month" title="Premier League Manager of the Month">Premier League Manager of the Month</a> award for December.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FA_Premier_League_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-FA_Premier_League-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>City's Premier League form tailed off again in the new year, with City jointly contesting the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_FA_Cup" title="2010–11 FA Cup">FA Cup</a> and Europa League, and Mancini cited burnout for losing ground in the league title race.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> City were eventually eliminated from the Europa League by Ukrainian side <a href="/wiki/FC_Dynamo_Kyiv" title="FC Dynamo Kyiv">Dynamo Kyiv</a> in March, but his team replied strongly by winning eight out of the next ten matches, including an <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_FA_Cup#Semi-finals" title="2010–11 FA Cup">FA Cup semi-final</a> victory at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley</a> over local rivals Manchester United in April.</p>
<p>A win over Tottenham in May guaranteed City the opportunity to play <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2011–12 UEFA Champions League">Champions League football</a> the following season. This win was followed by City winning the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_FA_Cup" title="2010–11 FA Cup">FA Cup</a> with a 1–0 victory over <a href="/wiki/Stoke_City_F.C." title="Stoke City F.C.">Stoke City</a> in the following weekend's <a href="/wiki/2011_FA_Cup_Final" title="2011 FA Cup Final">final</a> at Wembley. This <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> triumph meant that Mancini joined five other <a href="/wiki/List_of_Manchester_City_F.C._managers" title="List of Manchester City F.C. managers">City managers</a> who have all won major honours, and it has finally ended the club's longest trophy drought in <a href="/wiki/History_of_Manchester_City_F.C." title="History of Manchester City F.C.">its history</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> Due to their late run of form, City finished third in the league ahead of <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> after a 2–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Bolton_Wanderers_F.C." title="Bolton Wanderers F.C.">Bolton Wanderers</a> on the last day of the season, thereby avoiding the need to participate in <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_UEFA_Champions_League#Play-off_round" title="2011–12 UEFA Champions League">play-off</a> round fixtures in order to progress to the group stages of the following season's <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2011–12 UEFA Champions League">Champions League competition</a>. Only goal difference separated City from achieving a second-place finish over Chelsea.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2011.E2.80.9312">2011–12</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roberto_Mancini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: 2011–12">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The club were quieter in the closed season transfer window than in previous years, with the club's spending of approximately £75 million more in line with the corresponding amounts spent by rivals Manchester United and <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a>. £60 million of this sum was used to purchase two players: <a href="/wiki/Sergio_Ag%C3%BCero" title="Sergio Agüero">Sergio Agüero</a>, for a club record fee, and <a href="/wiki/Samir_Nasri" title="Samir Nasri">Samir Nasri</a> from <a href="/wiki/Atl%C3%A9tico_Madrid" title="Atlético Madrid">Atlético Madrid</a> and Arsenal respectively. Other players purchased during the summer included <a href="/wiki/Ga%C3%ABl_Clichy" title="Gaël Clichy">Gaël Clichy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stefan_Savi%C4%87" title="Stefan Savić">Stefan Savić</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Owen_Hargreaves" title="Owen Hargreaves">Owen Hargreaves</a> joined on a free transfer after having been released by Manchester United. City began the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Premier_League" title="2011–12 Premier League">Premier League season</a> very strongly, winning 12 of their first 14 matches and scoring an impressive 48 goals while only conceding 13. These results left City undefeated and five points clear at the top of the league over second-placed Manchester United by the beginning of December.</p>
<p>A revitalised <a href="/wiki/Edin_D%C5%BEeko" title="Edin Džeko">Edin Džeko</a> won the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Player_of_the_Month" title="Premier League Player of the Month">Premier League Player of the Month</a> award for August 2011, and David Silva won the same award for September 2011. Many were impressed with the impact of Agüero and Nasri, which had given City an exciting, attacking verve.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> Mancini was also responsible for inflicting United's worst loss since 1955 when his City side won 6–1 away at <a href="/wiki/Old_Trafford" title="Old Trafford">Old Trafford</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> He was named Premier League Manager of the Month as a result of City's strong form in the month of October.</p>
<p>City maintained the lead in the Premier League over the next five months but struggled in the Champions League in <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_UEFA_Champions_League_group_stage#Group_A" title="2011–12 UEFA Champions League group stage">group</a> that involved <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Bayern Munich">Bayern Munich</a>, <a href="/wiki/S.S.C._Napoli" title="S.S.C. Napoli">Napoli</a> and <a href="/wiki/Villarreal_CF" title="Villarreal CF">Villarreal</a>. City failed to progress, but finished third in the group with ten points, normally enough to guarantee qualification into the knock-out stages.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mancini_Nasri_Aguero.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1166" data-file-width="1882" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Mancini_Nasri_Aguero.JPG/220px-Mancini_Nasri_Aguero.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Mancini_Nasri_Aguero.JPG/330px-Mancini_Nasri_Aguero.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Mancini_Nasri_Aguero.JPG/440px-Mancini_Nasri_Aguero.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mancini_Nasri_Aguero.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mancini (left), <a href="/wiki/Samir_Nasri" title="Samir Nasri">Samir Nasri</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sergio_Ag%C3%BCero" title="Sergio Agüero">Sergio Agüero</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League trophy</a> during Manchester City's victory parade, May 2012.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A 3–2 loss to Manchester United in the FA Cup <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_FA_Cup" title="2011–12 FA Cup">third round</a> on 8 January 2012 was bittersweet. City had <a href="/wiki/Vincent_Kompany" title="Vincent Kompany">Vincent Kompany</a> controversially sent-off in the sixth minute and United managed to create a 3–0 lead before half-time against a lacklustre and beleaguered City team. However, after numerous tactical changes from Mancini at half-time, City came out fighting with ten men, a shadow of the team that played in the first half.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> Two goals from Aleksandar Kolarov and Sergio Agüero narrowed the deficit to just one goal. City were in the ascendency and continued to push for an equalising despite having only ten men, but failed to do so with the final whistle. Mancini later believed the match was a seminal moment in the development of his team, demonstrating that City were a better team than United. He believed that the match helped to carve out a fighting spirit that his team had previously lacked.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>City also progressed to the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Football_League_Cup#Semi-finals" title="2011–12 Football League Cup">League Cup semi-final</a>, maintaining Mancini's record of reaching a major competition semi-final in every season he has managed. City played Liverpool and conceded an away goal in the first leg with a penalty from <a href="/wiki/Steven_Gerrard" title="Steven Gerrard">Steven Gerrard</a>. City went to Anfield and led twice with goals from <a href="/wiki/Nigel_de_Jong" title="Nigel de Jong">Nigel de Jong</a> and Edin Džeko, but another penalty from <a href="/wiki/Steven_Gerrard" title="Steven Gerrard">Steven Gerrard</a> and a goal from <a href="/wiki/Craig_Bellamy" title="Craig Bellamy">Craig Bellamy</a> meant Liverpool won 3–2 on aggregate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> On 13 May 2012, City clinched the Premier League title in a dramatic 3–2 win over <a href="/wiki/Queens_Park_Rangers_F.C." title="Queens Park Rangers F.C.">Queens Park Rangers</a> after originally being 2–1 down going into injury time. He became the second Italian manager to win a Premier League title after <a href="/wiki/Carlo_Ancelotti" title="Carlo Ancelotti">Carlo Ancelotti</a>'s Chelsea team in <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Premier_League" title="2009–10 Premier League">2009–10</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2012.E2.80.9313">2012–13</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roberto_Mancini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: 2012–13">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Mancini stated pre-season that Manchester City's long-term aim was to win the Champions League.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Mancini declared that he envisaged less transfer activity in the summer, and is content with his attacking strikers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> On 9 July 2012, City announced that Roberto Mancini had signed a new five-year deal, meaning that he is contracted with the club until summer 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> City began the new season by participating in, and winning, the <a href="/wiki/2012_FA_Community_Shield" title="2012 FA Community Shield">2012 FA Community Shield</a> against <a href="/wiki/2012_FA_Cup_Final" title="2012 FA Cup Final">2012 FA Cup winners</a> Chelsea on 12 August 2012 at <a href="/wiki/Villa_Park" title="Villa Park">Villa Park</a>. Manchester City won 3–2 on this occasion. On 21 November 2012, a 1–1 draw at home to <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_C.F." title="Real Madrid C.F.">Real Madrid</a> saw Manchester City and Mancini exit the Champions League at the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_UEFA_Champions_League_group_stage#Group_D" title="2012–13 UEFA Champions League group stage">group stage</a> for the second successive season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the end of the calendar year of 2012, Manchester City were second in the Premier League, seven points behind local rivals Manchester United. In contrast to the 2011–12 league season, Mancini's team struggled to score sufficient goals and suffered some poor results in the second half of the season, such as a 3–1 loss to <a href="/wiki/Southampton_F.C." title="Southampton F.C.">Southampton</a> on 9 February 2013 (which Mancini described as the worst performance during his time in charge at City) and a 2–0 loss to <a href="/wiki/Everton_F.C." title="Everton F.C.">Everton</a> on 16 March. City's poor form led to United capturing the Premier League title on 22 April with a 3–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Aston_Villa_F.C." title="Aston Villa F.C.">Aston Villa</a> with four games to spare. On 11 May, Manchester City lost to Wigan Athletic 1–0 in the <a href="/wiki/2013_FA_Cup_Final" title="2013 FA Cup Final">2013 FA Cup Final</a>, with a late goal from Wigan's <a href="/wiki/Ben_Watson_(footballer,_born_July_1985)" title="Ben Watson (footballer, born July 1985)">Ben Watson</a>.</p>
<p>On 14 May, Mancini was sacked as manager of Manchester City two days after City's loss to Wigan in the FA Cup Final.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Roberto_Mancini:_Manchester_City_sack_manager_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-Roberto_Mancini:_Manchester_City_sack_manager-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> Aside from the season's poor European showing and timid league defence, it was reported that Mancini's relationship with the board and indeed his players had deteriorated to the point of no return.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> Speculation over Mancini's future had mounted for months beforehand; a question regarding then-<a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1laga_CF" title="Málaga CF">Málaga</a> manager <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Pellegrini" title="Manuel Pellegrini">Manuel Pellegrini</a> possibly taking Mancini's job in February 2013 provoked an expletive response from Mancini during a press conference.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> Mancini's public criticism of backroom and playing staff, as well as his distant relationships, alienated the players and the club hierarchy during the last eight months of his tenure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> On sacking Mancini, the club cited the need for a more "holistic" approach for the long-term future of the club, namely a manager passionate for developing players at youth level to create a "one house football club," as City look to open their new £100 million youth academy at the <a href="/wiki/Etihad_Campus" title="Etihad Campus">Etihad Campus</a> in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> With Manchester City, Mancini achieved the fourth-best win percentage in Premier League history, behind only <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mourinho" title="José Mourinho">José Mourinho</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alex_Ferguson" title="Alex Ferguson">Alex Ferguson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carlo_Ancelotti" title="Carlo Ancelotti">Carlo Ancelotti</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>A week after his sacking, Mancini took out a full page advert in the <i><a href="/wiki/Manchester_Evening_News" title="Manchester Evening News">Manchester Evening News</a></i> to say farewell and thank the club's fans – an act that was reciprocated in the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gazzetta_dello_Sport" title="Gazzetta dello Sport">Gazzetta dello Sport</a></i> by Manchester City supporters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Galatasaray">Galatasaray</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roberto_Mancini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Galatasaray">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roberto_Mancini%2713-14.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1276" data-file-width="688" height="408" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Roberto_Mancini%2713-14.JPG/220px-Roberto_Mancini%2713-14.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Roberto_Mancini%2713-14.JPG/330px-Roberto_Mancini%2713-14.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Roberto_Mancini%2713-14.JPG/440px-Roberto_Mancini%2713-14.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Roberto_Mancini%2713-14.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mancini managing <a href="/wiki/Galatasaray_S.K._(football)" title="Galatasaray S.K. (football)">Galatasaray</a> in 2013</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 30 September 2013, Mancini signed a three-year contract with Turkish side <a href="/wiki/Galatasaray_S.K._(football)" title="Galatasaray S.K. (football)">Galatasaray</a>, taking over from the previous coach <a href="/wiki/Fatih_Terim" title="Fatih Terim">Fatih Terim</a>, who had left to take over as coach of the <a href="/wiki/Turkey_national_football_team" title="Turkey national football team">Turkish national team</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Roberto_Mancini:_Galatasaray_appoint_ex-Man_City_boss_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-Roberto_Mancini:_Galatasaray_appoint_ex-Man_City_boss-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> In his first game in charge, on 2 October against <a href="/wiki/Juventus_F.C." title="Juventus F.C.">Juventus</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2013–14 UEFA Champions League">2013–14 Champions League</a>, Galatasaray drew 2–2 with a late equaliser.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> After a convincing 3–1 victory at home against <a href="/wiki/F.C._Copenhagen" title="F.C. Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a> in the same competition, his Galatasaray side this time defeated reigning Italian champions Juventus 1–0 on the crucial matchday six to advance to the last 16 of the tournament, a feat he was unable to achieve with Manchester City over two seasons. Galatasaray there met Chelsea and were eliminated despite drawing the home leg 1–1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>Under Mancini, Galatasaray won their first 12 <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_S%C3%BCper_Lig" title="2013–14 Süper Lig">2013–14 Süper Lig</a> home matches, including a 6–0 victory over <a href="/wiki/Bursaspor" title="Bursaspor">Bursaspor</a>, the highest winning margin in the league as of game week 20.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> On 7 May, Galatasaray won 1–0 against <a href="/wiki/Eski%C5%9Fehirspor" title="Eskişehirspor">Eskişehirspor</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Turkish_Cup" title="2013–14 Turkish Cup">2014 Turkish Cup Final</a> with a late goal from <a href="/wiki/Wesley_Sneijder" title="Wesley Sneijder">Wesley Sneijder</a>. On 11 June, Mancini left the club by mutual consent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Roberto_Mancini:_Galatasaray_manager_leaves_club_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-Roberto_Mancini:_Galatasaray_manager_leaves_club-92">[92]</a></sup> It has been reported by the club's chairman and the spokesperson that the club's transfer policy and the overall budget of the upcoming season was the reason behind the dispute. This was also verified by Mancini: "When I accepted the coaching post, Gala's aims were different."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Return_to_Inter">Return to Inter</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roberto_Mancini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Return to Inter">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 14 November 2014, Mancini agreed to a surprise return at his previous club Inter, replacing <a href="/wiki/Walter_Mazzarri" title="Walter Mazzarri">Walter Mazzarri</a> at the helm of the <i>Nerazzurri</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Inter_Milan_confirm_Roberto_Mancini_appointment_after_Walter_Mazzarri_exit_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-Inter_Milan_confirm_Roberto_Mancini_appointment_after_Walter_Mazzarri_exit-94">[94]</a></sup> His first game in charge was against rivals <a href="/wiki/A.C._Milan" title="A.C. Milan">A.C. Milan</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Derby_della_Madonnina" title="Derby della Madonnina">Derby della Madonnina</a>, which finished in a 1–1 draw, with the club's goal scored by <a href="/wiki/Joel_Obi" title="Joel Obi">Joel Obi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> On 27 November 2014, Mancini's 50th birthday, Inter played the first European match of his second spell, a 2–1 home win over <a href="/wiki/FC_Dnipro_Dnipropetrovsk" title="FC Dnipro Dnipropetrovsk">Dnipro Dnipropetrovsk</a> to confirm that Inter would top the group with a game remaining.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 8 August 2016 Mancini left Inter on a mutual agreement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Management_style">Management style</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roberto_Mancini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Management style">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Despite having been being a support striker during his playing career, Mancini places great emphasis on building from the back, stressing the importance of not conceding a goal means the team will always have an opportunity to win, going as far to say, "I like 1–0 wins. When you don't concede a goal and you have players like <a href="/wiki/Edin_D%C5%BEeko" title="Edin Džeko">Edin Džeko</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Tevez" title="Carlos Tevez">Carlos Tevez</a> or <a href="/wiki/David_Silva" title="David Silva">David Silva</a>, you win 90%. I prefer we are boring for two to three matches and we win 1–0. If you watch teams that won titles, they conceded very few goals."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> Despite this, some argue Mancini is more of a "defence first" manager rather than a "win first" manager,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> a style that has been criticised by some in the <a href="/wiki/Media_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Media of the United Kingdom">British media</a>. Others accepted that his pragmatic and cautious approach was what the team lacked, and that Mancini's style would ensure City could challenge for trophies regularly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<p>At Manchester City, Mancini had inherited a team from <a href="/wiki/Mark_Hughes" title="Mark Hughes">Mark Hughes</a>, which while showing great prolificacy and potential in front of goal, had an insecure defence. Intensively coaching his defence enabled him to get his tenure at City off to a positive start. In Inter's <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_Serie_A" title="2007–08 Serie A">2007–08</a> Serie A-winning season, Inter conceded the fewest goals in the league with 26, 11 fewer than <a href="/wiki/Juventus_F.C." title="Juventus F.C.">Juventus</a> and <a href="/wiki/A.S._Roma" title="A.S. Roma">Roma</a>, and at City, his team gradually garnered a reputation as being well organised defensively and tough to break down. In Mancini's first full season in charge at City, they conceded 33 goals in the Premier League, the fewest along with Chelsea and 18 clean sheets, the highest in the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Premier_League" title="2010–11 Premier League">2010–11 Premier League season</a>.</p>
<p>Mancini's training methods have been criticised by some City players<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> and especially by ex-Manchester City fitness coach <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Verheijen" title="Raymond Verheijen">Raymond Verheijen</a>, who is a personal fitness coach for <a href="/wiki/Craig_Bellamy" title="Craig Bellamy">Craig Bellamy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> During his time at City, Mancini tried to stamp his authority with rebellious players who were not performing well and has stated, "If a top player is not happy then it's better to go."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<p>Mancini is known to use the media to alleviate the pressure from his players. Following City's defeat to <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Premier_League" title="2011–12 Premier League">2011–12 season</a>, a deficit of eight points had been established between rivals <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> with only six matches left to play. After the Arsenal match, he believed the deficit was catchable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> City, however, won the next match convincingly against <a href="/wiki/West_Bromwich_Albion_F.C." title="West Bromwich Albion F.C.">West Bromwich Albion</a> 4–0, but from then on Mancini maintained in post-match interviews that the title race was over.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> City won the next three matches, meaning a win against Manchester United would put them top of the league on goal difference. City beat United 1–0, with Mancini conceding the title race was back on – but that United were favourites with two matches to play.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> Mancini's unorthodox approach worked, and City won the league on goal difference with 89 points after six consecutive league wins in the final six matches. Mancini's players believed his approach alleviated pressure and helped City to win the last six league matches, which won the title on goal difference.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> Mancini stated afterwards that he always believed personally that City could win the title, but wanted his players to prove they could despite his public statements suggesting otherwise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversy">Controversy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roberto_Mancini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Controversy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>There was much controversy surrounding <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_football_team" title="Italy national football team">Italy</a>'s <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016_qualifying" title="UEFA Euro 2016 qualifying">UEFA Euro 2016 qualifying</a> match on 28 March 2015 against <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria_national_football_team" title="Bulgaria national football team">Bulgaria</a>, as Italy head coach <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Conte" title="Antonio Conte">Antonio Conte</a> called up Brazilian-born <a href="/wiki/%C3%89der_(Italian_footballer)" title="Éder (Italian footballer)">Éder</a> and Argentine-born <a href="/wiki/Franco_V%C3%A1zquez" title="Franco Vázquez">Franco Vázquez</a>. Both players hold an Italian citizenship as they have relatives that are Italian, allowing them to be eligible to play for Italy. Speaking at a Serie A meeting on 23 March 2015, Mancini said, "The Italian national team should be Italian. An Italian player deserves to play for the national team while someone who wasn't born in Italy, even if they have relatives, I don't think they deserve to."</p>
<p>Conte's response to the use of foreign-born players was, "If <a href="/wiki/Mauro_Camoranesi" title="Mauro Camoranesi">Mauro Camoranesi</a> [who was born in Argentina] was allowed to help Italy win the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 World Cup</a>, then why can't Éder and Franco Vázquez lead the Azzurri to glory in <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016" title="UEFA Euro 2016">next year's European Championship</a>?"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following a heated exchange between Mancini and <a href="/wiki/S.S.C._Napoli" title="S.S.C. Napoli">Napoli</a> coach <a href="/wiki/Maurizio_Sarri" title="Maurizio Sarri">Maurizio Sarri</a> in the final minutes of a <a href="/wiki/Coppa_Italia" title="Coppa Italia">Coppa Italia</a> match on 20 January 2016, Mancini accused Sarri of being a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Homophobe" title="Homophobe">homophobe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> Sarri responded to the accusations by affirming that he wasn't a homophobe, and that "what happens on the field, stays on the field".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> Sarri was consequently fined €20,000 and banned for two Coppa Italia matches by <a href="/wiki/Lega_Serie_A" title="Lega Serie A">Lega Serie A</a> for "directing extremely insulting epithets at the coach of the opposing team".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roberto_Mancini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Mancini has been married for nearly 28 years to Federica. He is a Catholic, was an altar boy as a child in <a href="/wiki/Ancona" title="Ancona">Ancona</a> and still attends <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholic_mass" title="Catholic mass">mass</a> regularly with his family.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> The couple have a daughter and two sons, <a href="/wiki/Filippo_Mancini" title="Filippo Mancini">Filippo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andrea_Mancini" title="Andrea Mancini">Andrea</a>, who have both played in the <a href="/wiki/F.C._Internazionale_Milano_Primavera" title="F.C. Internazionale Milano Primavera">Inter youth</a> ranks, where Filippo has played ten minutes in a Coppa Italia match. Both of his sons have at one point been a part of <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C._Reserves_and_Academy" title="Manchester City F.C. Reserves and Academy">Manchester City's under-21 youth team</a>. Filippo trained with the club's youth/reserve team for several months during the 2007–08 season before Roberto was appointed as City's manager, while Andrea was signed by his father for the <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C._Reserves_and_Academy#Elite_Development_Squad" title="Manchester City F.C. Reserves and Academy">Elite Development Squad</a> in November 2010 after being released from <a href="/wiki/Bologna_F.C._1909" title="Bologna F.C. 1909">Bologna</a>. <a href="/wiki/Andrea_Mancini" title="Andrea Mancini">Andrea</a> was released at the end of the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Premier_League" title="2011–12 Premier League">2011–12</a> season.</p>
<p>Mancini was estimated to have a personal wealth of £19 million in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> Mancini has joked about watching the soap opera <i><a href="/wiki/Coronation_Street" title="Coronation Street">Coronation Street</a></i> to help improve his English.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> Mancini has maintained a tradition of wearing a scarf of his club's colours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career_statistics">Career statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roberto_Mancini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Career statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="International_goals">International goals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Roberto_Mancini&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: International goals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>

<tr>
